# Dashboard PRD Plan: Treasury Surfaces

**Source:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md`
**Generated:** 2026-04-25
**Source hash:** `5df3ebf3da6047ee9d6607c067cd2ff4eea69a52a3febd1a28bcdcf13b6c63f8`
**Section tasks:** 65
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/chain.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/feeds.rs`
- `crates/roko-chain/src/`

### DASH-17-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:7` through `28`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

Treasury is the section where the economic reality of operating on Nunchi is made legible. Two distinct concerns live here:

First, operational economics: how much does running your agents cost, and how is that cost distributed. This is the Cost Analytics surface and is used heavily by Solo Operators and Fleet Orchestrators.

Second, product-facing economics: positions in tradable instruments, the ISFR benchmark rate, cross-chain state, and the yield perpetual market. This is the trading and product-consumption surface used by users of the yield products.

These two concerns are related (both are "money flowing through the system") but serve different personas and different activities. The Treasury section holds both but separates them clearly.

Treasury contains five pages:

- **Positions** — active holdings in yield perpetuals and other tradable instruments.
- **Cost Analytics** — aggregate cost tracking across agents, providers, time.
- **ISFR Dashboard** — the benchmark rate, its components, its history.
- **Multi-Chain** — cross-chain state and bridge flows.
- **Yield Perpetuals** — the dedicated trading and hedging surface for yield perps.

Primary personas for Treasury: Solo Operator and Fleet Orchestrator (Cost Analytics), traders and Passive Users (Positions, Yield Perpetuals, ISFR), anyone managing multi-chain state (Multi-Chain).

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `192`
- Section hash: `4ed82d18180e46d8fbd74fdbdcd39021305cabe10f6611f9c6fc3ba82c595b14`

**Normative requirements and implementation claims:**
- Second, product-facing economics: positions in tradable instruments, the ISFR benchmark rate, cross-chain state, and the yield perpetual market. This is the trading and product-consumption surface used by users of the yield products.
- - **Positions** — active holdings in yield perpetuals and other tradable instruments. - **Cost Analytics** — aggregate cost tracking across agents, providers, time. - **ISFR Dashboard** — the benchmark rate, its components, its history. - **Multi-Chain** — cross-chain state and bridge flows. - **Yield Perpetuals** — the dedicated trading and hedging surface for yield perps.
- Primary personas for Treasury: Solo Operator and Fleet Orchestrator (Cost Analytics), traders and Passive Users (Positions, Yield Perpetuals, ISFR), anyone managing multi-chain state (Multi-Chain).
- ---

````markdown
Filterable and sortable.

- Opened.
- Adjusted.
- Closed.

Each entry links to the transaction detail.
````

### DASH-17-S010 -- Interactions

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:98` through `104`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click a position: navigate to Position Detail (drill-down with full history, price chart, risk metrics).
- Actions: manage (route to Yield Perpetuals if that's the instrument type), close (confirmation flow), view on chain.
- Filters: by instrument type, by chain, by age.
- Export: CSV of position history.
````

### DASH-17-S021 -- Section 02 — Cost by agent

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:171` through `210`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Section 02 — Cost by agent

A breakdown of cost attributed to each agent, as a bar chart or sortable list. Agents with the highest cost are most visible.

Each entry: agent, portrait, today's cost, 7d cost, trend, percent of total.

**Section 03 — Cost by provider.**

A similar breakdown but by LLM provider. Shows which providers are costing the most, which are trending up, which are providing best value per dollar.

**Section 04 — Cost efficiency.**

A measure of cost per meaningful outcome:

- Cost per episode.
- Cost per successful gate pass.
- Cost per knowledge entry promoted.
- Cost per arena point earned.

These numbers matter more than raw cost — they show whether agents are producing value commensurate with their expense.

Trends over time highlight improvement or decline.

**Section 05 — Cascade effectiveness.**

A panel showing how well the cascade router is saving cost. Percentage of ticks handled at T0 (free), T1 (cheap), T2 (expensive). Savings estimate compared to a baseline "all T2" configuration.

This quantifies the value of scaffolding (thesis 1) in dollars.

**Section 06 — Budget limits and alerts.**

User-configurable budget caps:

- Daily cap.
- Weekly cap.
- Monthly cap.
- Per-agent caps.

With status indicators (green/amber/red) showing how close each is to its limit.
````

````markdown
### Purpose

The Interest-bearing Stablecoin Funding Rate. A benchmark rate computed on-chain at consensus from a basket of sources. This page makes the ISFR legible — its current value, its history, its components, its implied curves.

The ISFR is a product-critical number. It is the reference rate for Korai-native yield products and the ground truth source for several evals.
````

### DASH-17-S033 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:280` through `325`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — ISFR hero.**

- Current ISFR rate (mono, very large, live-ticking).
- 24h change.
- 7d change.
- Time since last oracle update.

**Section 01 — ISFR history chart.**

A line chart showing ISFR over time. Selectable windows (24h, 7d, 30d, all time). Annotations for significant events (protocol upgrades, market shocks).

**Section 02 — Components.**

The ISFR is computed from a basket of source rates. This section shows each component:

- Source name (e.g., "Aave USDC rate," "Compound USDC rate," "MakerDAO DSR").
- Current value.
- Weight in the composite.
- Last update time.
- Reliability indicator.

Visualized as a weighted stack, where the stack height is the ISFR and each segment is a component.

**Section 03 — Implied curves.**

Derived curves from ISFR data:

- Forward rate curve.
- Term structure implied by yield perpetual prices.
- Spread vs other benchmarks.

For trading users, these curves are load-bearing.

**Section 04 — Recent oracle updates.**

A feed of recent oracle update events:

- Timestamp.
- New value.
- Attesting validators.
- Block number.

Verifiable against on-chain state.
````

````markdown
### Purpose

Cross-chain state. The dashboard primarily lives on Korai (or Mirage), but users may have assets on other chains, may bridge assets, may monitor cross-chain flows. This page surfaces multi-chain state.

This page is thin in the current dashboard. Whether to invest more depends on how important cross-chain is to the near-term product. This specification provides a capable structure; depth is configurable.
````

````markdown
- Status (pending, complete, failed).
- Transaction links.

**Section 04 — Agent cross-chain activity.**

- Which agents interact with which chains.
- Chain-specific agent capabilities.
- Recent cross-chain agent actions.
````

### DASH-17-S053 -- Purpose

````markdown
### Purpose

Dedicated trading and hedging surface for yield perpetuals. Where users can trade perp contracts settling against ISFR or other yield benchmarks, manage their yield-perp positions, see clearing rounds, and interact with the cooperative clearing engine.

This is a new page in this specification. In the current dashboard, yield perp activity is mentioned but not surfaced as a dedicated trading surface. Given its likely importance to the product's economic story, making it a dedicated page is recommended.
````

### DASH-17-S057 -- Page sections

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:503` through `555`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page sections

**Section 00 — Yield Perpetuals header.**

Title, italic-serif description: *"Trade the benchmark rate. Hedge yield. Participate in cooperative clearing."*

Summary strip:

- ISFR current.
- Total open interest.
- Recent clearing rounds.
- Next clearing in: countdown.

**Section 01 — Market.**

The trading interface:

- Instrument selector (different yield perps by tenor, by underlying benchmark).
- Current price.
- Order book (simplified given cooperative clearing is not an order-book mechanism, but a "current bids and offers" view is useful).
- Entry UI: long or short, size, limit or market, slippage tolerance.
- Clearing history for this instrument.

**Section 02 — My positions.**

User's open yield perp positions (also shown under Positions page, but restricted here to yield perps). Each with:

- Instrument.
- Side.
- Size.
- Entry price.
- Mark price.
- Unrealized P&L.
- Funding paid/received.
- Actions (close, partial close, adjust).

**Section 03 — Clearing rounds.**

A feed of clearing rounds:

- Round number.
- Clearing timestamp.
- Clearing price.
- Total volume cleared.
- Your participation.
- Link to the on-chain clearing event.

Clearing is periodic (e.g., every 30 minutes or every N blocks). A countdown shows when the next round happens.

**Section 04 — ISFR curve and implied.**

A view showing ISFR's current value and the implied curve from yield perp prices at different tenors. Essential context for traders.
````

### DASH-17-S064 -- Shared patterns across Treasury

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:600` through `613`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Shared patterns across Treasury

**Chain Lens dominates.** Most Treasury pages are Chain Lens primary, with Fleet Lens as the user-scoped alternative. The exception is Cost Analytics, which is Fleet-first because it's about off-chain operational cost.

**Real-time is critical.** Prices, values, positions update continuously. Staleness is more dangerous here than in most sections — a stale ISFR value or a stale position value could lead to bad decisions.

**On-chain writes are common.** Many Treasury actions (opening a position, bridging, closing a trade) involve on-chain transactions. These require confirmation dialogs with gas estimates, simulation results, and explicit user signing per `06-navigation-and-traversal.md`.

**Cost and value are distinct.** Cost Analytics is about operational expense (the cost of running agents). Positions, ISFR, and Yield Perpetuals are about financial value (what the user holds, what things are worth). Confusing them would be a design failure.

**Privacy matters.** A user's positions and cost are their private data. Even in Global Lens on these pages, the user's own holdings remain private; only aggregates or user-opted public data is shown.

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `180`
- Section hash: `fc7e8dcdf64a008062ed9cd1f5e4b456a6e3e76106d61bc6ec1af895a8ff992f`

**Normative requirements and implementation claims:**
- **Chain Lens dominates.** Most Treasury pages are Chain Lens primary, with Fleet Lens as the user-scoped alternative. The exception is Cost Analytics, which is Fleet-first because it's about off-chain operational cost.
- **Real-time is critical.** Prices, values, positions update continuously. Staleness is more dangerous here than in most sections — a stale ISFR value or a stale position value could lead to bad decisions.
- **On-chain writes are common.** Many Treasury actions (opening a position, bridging, closing a trade) involve on-chain transactions. These require confirmation dialogs with gas estimates, simulation results, and explicit user signing per `06-navigation-and-traversal.md`.
- **Cost and value are distinct.** Cost Analytics is about operational expense (the cost of running agents). Positions, ISFR, and Yield Perpetuals are about financial value (what the user holds, what things are worth). Confusing them would be a design failure.
- **Privacy matters.** A user's positions and cost are their private data. Even in Global Lens on these pages, the user's own holdings remain private; only aggregates or user-opted public data is shown.
- ---

### DASH-17-S065 -- Deferred across Treasury

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/17-treasury-surfaces.md:614` through `620`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Deferred across Treasury

- **Portfolio analytics:** sophisticated portfolio metrics (Sharpe, Sortino, drawdown analysis). Basic P&L; advanced portfolio analytics deferred.
- **Tax preparation:** tax-ready exports, cost basis tracking. Deferred.
- **Automated strategies:** yield-maximizing strategies that automatically rebalance positions. Deferred to strategy-marketplace workstream.
- **Structured products:** packaged products combining multiple primitives (e.g., "3x leveraged ISFR exposure"). Deferred.
- **Fiat on/off ramps:** integrating fiat deposit/withdrawal. Usually handled by wallet providers; deferred.
````

- Section word count: `67`
